## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws and concentration-time dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is a time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics where reaction mechanisms induce characteristic rate-law dependencies on A and sometimes explicit time dependence via forcing, catalyst activity, or approach to equilibrium.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption of A, e.g., surface-limited with excess reactant)
- Zero-order with source term: dA_dt = c0 - c1 (net constant production/consumption over the observation window)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- First-order to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular consumption with A as the limiting reactant)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global order kinetics)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-like consumption or growth: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating kinetics with depletion/limitation)
- Competing formation and decay: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant feed/formation with first-order loss)
- Inhibited (crowding/product inhibition) rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A + 1) (rate suppressed at high A by an inhibition term)
- Mixed-order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order loss processes)
- Time-varying activity (catalyst deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (effective rate constant decays over time)
- Stretched-exponential time dependence (distributed kinetics): dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t**c2) (non-single-timescale deactivation/aging effects)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., light modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) (rate modulated by an external periodic driver)
- Finite-time singular/empirical acceleration: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (t + c1) (apparent rate decreases with time due to changing conditions like dilution or activity loss)
- Empirical rational rate law: dA_dt = -(c0 * A + c1 * A**2) / (c2 * A + 1) (interpolates between low- and high-A limiting kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification: dependence dA_dt ∝ A, A**2, or A**c indicates first-, second-, or n-th order kinetics, respectively.
- Equilibrium approach: a factor (A - c) implies relaxation toward a steady-state/equilibrium concentration c with characteristic timescale set by the prefactor.
- Parallel pathways: additive loss terms (A and A**2 together) suggest multiple mechanisms operating simultaneously (e.g., unimolecular + bimolecular).
- Autocatalysis/feedback: multiplicative form A*(c - A) indicates self-acceleration at low A with depletion/limitation at high A, often yielding sigmoidal A(t).
- Inhibition or crowding: rational suppression A/(1 + c*A) indicates an effective rate constant that decreases as A increases (product inhibition, site blocking).
- Time-varying environment: multiplicative exp(-c*t) or exp(-c*t**p) on the rate indicates changing catalyst activity, temperature programs, or aging effects.
- External driving: sinusoidal dependence on t indicates periodically varying rate conditions (illumination, mixing cycles, pulsed inputs).
- Net production vs consumption: presence of a positive constant/source term alongside -c*A indicates feed/formation balancing decay, leading to a nonzero steady A.
- Apparent time-dependent rate constants: factors like 1/(t + c) represent effective kinetic parameters that drift over time due to unmodeled processes (dilution, adsorption, fouling).
